9:[["$","meta","0",{"name":"viewport","content":"width=device-width, initial-scale=1"}],["$","meta","1",{"charSet":"utf-8"}],["$","title","2",{"children":"D10f | Modifying HTTP Responses On The Fly"}],["$","meta","3",{"name":"description","content":"Nginx's JavaScript engine can be used to modify request &amp; responses on the fly. 1:null
a:I[3475,["750","static/chunks/750-0f816d740819c251.js","308","static/chunks/app/blog/%5Bslug%5D/page-920a7887c59b1504.js"],"default"]
b:T795f5,<div id="preamble">
<div class="sectionbody">
<div class="paragraph">
<p>The Nginx JavaScript engine, "njs", is available out of the box in most distributions as well as in the latest Docker image.</p>
</div>
</div>
</div><menu class="toc"><li class="toc__item"><a href="#_example_1_setting_response_headers_dynamically">Example 1: Setting Response Headers Dynamically</a><ul><li class="toc__item"><a href="#_format_the_date_strings">Format The Date Strings</a></li><li class="toc__item"><a href="#_computing_the_date_from_query_parameters">Computing The Date From Query Parameters</a></li><li class="toc__item"><a href="#_putting_it_all_together">Putting It All Together</a></li></ul></li><li class="toc__item"><a href="#_example_2_runtime_environment_variables">Example 2: Runtime Environment Variables</a><ul><li class="toc__item"><a href="#_deploying_with_docker">Deploying With Docker</a></li><li class="toc__item"><a href="#_inject_environment_variables_dynamically">Inject Environment Variables Dynamically</a></li><li class="toc__item"><a href="#_cleaning_up_things_a_little">Cleaning Up Things A Little</a></li></ul></li></menu>
<div class="sect1"><h2 id="_example_1_setting_response_headers_dynamically">Example 1: Setting Response Headers Dynamically<a class="anchor" href="#_example_1_setting_response_headers_dynamically">
                    <svg aria-hidden="true">
                        <use href="/sprite.svg#icon-link" />
                    </svg>
                </a></h2>
<div class="sectionbody">
<div class="paragraph">
<p>First, let me give you some context.</p>
</div>
<div class="paragraph">
<p>Recently, I&#8217;ve been working on making an HTTP client in Python. I used Nginx running inside a Docker container to make sure basic requests were working properly. At one point I needed to test if redirects and rate limiting responses were handled properly, both of which may include the header "Retry-After".</p>
</div>
<div class="paragraph">
<p>This header specifies the time that the client must wait before making another request to the server. How it does that precisely is defined in <a href="https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc9110.html#name-date-time-formats">RFC9110</a>, using what&#8217;s called an "IMF-fixdate" format. However, this RFC also states that a client must accept another two now-obsolete formats, still considered for backwards compatibility.</p>
</div>
<div class="paragraph">
<p>Since these headers needed to specify dates into the future, I had to edit the configuration file inside the Docker container, reload the server, and run my script to make sure it waited to appropriate amount of time. Very tedious and time-consuming, and exactly where <code>njs</code> comes in to the rescue.</p>
</div>
<div class="paragraph">
<p>The goal is to find a sweet spot of just a few seconds into the future so that I could know for sure my HTTP client worked properly, without having to wait for too long, so that I could iterate through my code as I fixed any bugs.</p>
</div>
<div class="sect2"><h3 id="_format_the_date_strings">Format The Date Strings<a class="anchor" href="#_format_the_date_strings">
                    <svg aria-hidden="true">
                        <use href="/sprite.svg#icon-link" />
                    </svg>
                </a></h3>
<div class="paragraph">
<p>For every request there must be a Retry-After header returning a date string formatted in one of the accepted formats:</p>
</div>
<div class="dlist">
<dl>
<dt class="hdlist1">Sun, 06 Nov 1994 08:49:37 GMT </dt>
<dd>
<p>A fixed-length and single-zone subset of the date and time specification used by the Internet Message Format in RFC5322.</p>
</dd>
<dt class="hdlist1">Sunday, 06-Nov-94 08:49:37 GMT </dt>
<dd>
<p>Format used in the now-obsolete RFC850.</p>
</dd>
<dt class="hdlist1">Sun Nov  6 08:49:37 1994 </dt>
<dd>
<p>An old format used by ANSI C&#8217;s asctime() function.</p>
</dd>
</dl>
</div>
<div class="paragraph">
<p>Let&#8217;s start by writing a few functions to handle this for the current date and time:</p>
</div>
<div class="codeblock">

                    </svg>

                        <use href="/sprite.svg#icon-clipboard-success" />
                    </svg>
                </span>
            </button>

                <i class="conum pr-2" data-value="1"></i>
                <b>â¶</b>
            </td>
            <td>Since all date formats have the same components arranged in different ways, we can parse any and extract the components we need. In this case, the IMF format is the easiest to compute.</td>

                <i class="conum pr-2" data-value="2"></i>
                <b>â·</b>
            </td>
            <td>Unfortunately, while <code>njs</code> has some convenient functionality like named capture groups, it does not yet support destructuring.</td>
        </tr>

                </table>

<div class="sect2"><h3 id="_computing_the_date_from_query_parameters">Computing The Date From Query Parameters<a class="anchor" href="#_computing_the_date_from_query_parameters">
                    <svg aria-hidden="true">
                        <use href="/sprite.svg#icon-link" />
                    </svg>
                </a></h3>
<div class="paragraph">
<p>Next, we need to be able to specify which format we want to return, and how much of an offset add to it. Both of these things can be done by introducing a new function that reads the query parameters from the request:</p>
</div>

            <button class="codeblock__copy-btn rotating-btn  js-required">

                        <use href="/sprite.svg#icon-clipboard-success" />
                    </svg>
                </span>
            </button>

                <span style="font-style: italic;"></span>
                <figure>

<span class="line"><span style="color:#CAD3F5;--shiki-catppuccin-light:#4C4F69;--shiki-catppuccin-dark:#C6D0F5;--shiki-everforest-dark:#D3C6AA;--shiki-everforest-light:#5C6A72;--shiki-solarized-light:#268BD2;--shiki-solarized-dark:#268BD2;--shiki-gruvbox-light:#076678;--shiki-gruvbox-dark:#83A598">            formattedDate</span><span style="color:#8BD5CA;--shiki-catppuccin-light:#179299;--shiki-catppuccin-dark:#81C8BE;--shiki-everforest-dark:#E69875;--shiki-everforest-light:#F57D26;--shiki-solarized-light:#859900;--shiki-solarized-dark:#859900;--shiki-gruvbox-light:#427B58;--shiki-gruvbox-dark:#8EC07C"> =</span><span style="color:#CAD3F5;--shiki-catppuccin-light:#4C4F69;--shiki-catppuccin-dark:#C6D0F5;--shiki-everforest-dark:#D3C6AA;--shiki-everforest-light:#5C6A72;--shiki-solarized-light:#268BD2;--shiki-solarized-dark:#268BD2;--shiki-gruvbox-light:#076678;--shiki-gruvbox-dark:#83A598"> amountInSeconds</span><span style="color:#939AB7;--shiki-catppuccin-light:#7C7F93;--shiki-catppuccin-dark:#949CBB;--shiki-everforest-dark:#D3C6AA;--shiki-everforest-light:#5C6A72;--shiki-solarized-light:#657B83;--shiki-solarized-dark:#839496;--shiki-gruvbox-light:#7C6F64;--shiki-gruvbox-dark:#A89984">;</span><span style="color:#CAD3F5;--shiki-catppuccin-light:#4C4F69;--shiki-catppuccin-dark:#C6D0F5;--shiki-everforest-dark:#D3C6AA;--shiki-everforest-light:#5C6A72;--shiki-solarized-light:#268BD2;--shiki-solarized-dark:#268BD2;--shiki-gruvbox-light:#076678;--shiki-gruvbox-dark:#83A598"><i class="conum pl-2" data-value="2"><b>â·</b></i></span></span>
<span class="line"><span style="color:#939AB7;--shiki-catppuccin-light:#7C7F93;--shiki-catppuccin-dark:#949CBB;--shiki-everforest-dark:#D3C6AA;--shiki-everforest-light:#5C6A72;--shiki-solarized-light:#657B83;--shiki-solarized-dark:#839496;--shiki-gruvbox-light:#7C6F64;--shiki-gruvbox-dark:#A89984">    }</span></span>
<span class="line"></span>
<span class="line"><span    r</span><span style="color:#CAD3F5;--shiki-catppuccin-light:#4C4F69;--shiki-catppuccin-dark:#C6D0F5;--shiki-everforest-dark:#D3C6AA;--shiki-everforest-light:#5C6A72;--shiki-solarized-light:#657B83;--shiki-solarized-dark:#839496;--shiki-gruvbox-light:#3C3836;--shiki-gruvbox-dark:#EBDBB2">]</span><span style="color:#8BD5CA;--shiki-catppuccin-light:#179299;--shiki-catppuccin-dark:#81C8BE;--shiki-everforest-dark:#E69875;--shiki-everforest-light:#F57D26;--shiki-solarized-light:#859900;--shiki-solarized-dark:#859900;--shiki-gruvbox-light:#427B58;--shiki-gruvbox-dark:#8EC07C"> =</span><span style="color:#CAD3F5;--shiki-catppuccin-light:#4C4F69;--shiki-catppuccin-dark:#C6D0F5;--shiki-everforest-dark:#D3C6AA;--shiki-everforest-light:#5C6A72;--shiki-solarized-light:#268BD2;--shiki-solarized-dark:#268BD2;--shiki-gruvbox-light:#076678;--shiki-gruvbox-dark:#83A598"> formattedDate</span><span style="color:#939AB7;--shiki-catppuccin-light:#7C7F93;--shiki-catppuccin-dark:#949CBB;--shiki-everforest-dark:#D3C6AA;--shiki-everforest-light:#5C6A72;--shiki-solarized-light:#657B83;--shiki-solarized-dark:#839496;--shiki-gruvbox-light:#7C6F64;--shiki-gruvbox-dark:#A89984">;</span></span>
<span class="line"><span style="color:#939AB7;--shiki-catppuccin-light:#7C7F93;--shiki-catppuccin-dark:#949CBB;--shiki-everforest-dark:#D3C6AA;--shiki-everforest-light:#5C6A72;--shiki-solarized-light:#657B83;--shiki-solarized-dark:#839496;--shiki-gruvbox-light:#7C6F64;--shiki-gruvbox-dark:#A89984">}</span></span></code></pre>
                </figure>
            </div>
        </div>
<div class="colist arabic">
                <table>
                    <tbody>
                        <tr>
            <td>
                <i class="conum pr-2" data-value="1"></i>
                <b>â¶</b>
            </td>
            <td>The "r" object, as it's commonly named in the Nginx documentation, represents the HTTP request.</td>
        </tr><tr>
            <td>
                <i class="conum pr-2" data-value="2"></i>
                <b>â·</b>
            </td>
            <td>The Retry-After header can also be expressed as seconds. When the date format is not specified, we assume this is the case.</td>
        </tr>
                    </tbody>
                </table>
            </div>
<div class="paragraph">
<p>This is the function that will be invoked from Nginx. It will read the query string for the request and decide based on the "format" and "amount" values the correct return value. Except, there&#8217;s really no return value since all we want to do is update the response headers. We can do that through the request object that gets passed automatically by Nginx, as seen at the bottom of the function.</p>
</div>
</div>
<div class="sect2"><h3 id="_putting_it_all_together">Putting It All Together<a class="anchor" href="#_putting_it_all_together">
                    <svg aria-hidden="true">
                        <use href="/sprite.svg#icon-link" />
                    </svg>
                </a></h3>
<div class="paragraph">
<p>And that&#8217;s really it. Now it&#8217;s a matter of wiring things up see if it works:</p>

        </div>
</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="sect1"><h2 id="_example_2_runtime_environment_variables">Example 2: Runtime Environment Variables<a class="anchor" href="#_example_2_runtime_environment_variables">
                    <svg aria-hidden="true">
                        <use href="/sprite.svg#icon-link" />
                    </svg>
                </a></h2>
<div class="sectionbody">
<div class="paragraph">
<p>I know, I know. Full-stack frameworks like Next.js are all the rage these days. But there are still valid reasons to use plain React to build simple, interactive web applications.</p>
</div>
<div class="paragraph">
<p>One of the many caveats that these web apps have, however, is they require a build step before they&#8217;re deployed. This makes things a bit more complicated than they need to be when there are changes unrelated to the business logic. This doesn&#8217;t necessarily mean sensitive information, like API keys. It could be simple values that remain constant throughout the lifetime of the application, locale changes, poll intervals, etc.</p>
</div>
<div class="paragraph">
<p>Consider as an example a file upload component. As with all user input, the validation will happen on the server side, but we want to give the user a good experience and inform them about errors when the file size is exceeded, or the file types is invalid. None of these are crucial, sensitive information, but having it kept in sync with our server is important.</p>
</div>
<div class="sect2"><h3 id="_deploying_with_docker">Deploying With Docker<a class="anchor" href="#_deploying_with_docker">
                    <svg aria-hidden="true">
                        <use href="/sprite.svg#icon-link" />
                    </svg>
                </a></h3>
<div class="paragraph">
<p>In this example, we deploy the client and the server using a Docker Compose file, something like this (simplified for brevity):</p>
</div>

            <button class="codeblock__copy-btn rotating-btn mt-6 js-required">

                    </svg>

                    <svg aria-hidden="true" style="transform: rotate(180deg);">
                        <use href="/sprite.svg#icon-clipboard-success" />
                    </svg>
                </span>
            </button>

<span class="line"><span style="color:#8AADF4;--shiki-catppuccin-light:#1E66F5;--shiki-catppuccin-dark:#8CAAEE;--shiki-everforest-dark:#E69875;--shiki-everforest-light:#F57D26;--shiki-solarized-light:#268BD2;--shiki-solarized-dark:#268BD2;--shiki-gruvbox-light:#427B58;--shiki-gruvbox-dark:#8EC07C">            context</span><span style="color:#8BD5CA;--shiki-catppuccin-light:#179299;--shiki-catppuccin-dark:#81C8BE;--shiki-everforest-dark:#859289;--shiki-everforest-light:#939F91;--shiki-solarized-light:#657B83;--shiki-solarized-dark:#839496;--shiki-gruvbox-light:#7C6F64;--shiki-gruvbox-dark:#A89984">:</span><span style="color:#A6DA95;--shiki-catppuccin-light:#40A02B;--shiki-catppuccin-dark:#A6D189;--shiki-everforest-dark:#A7C080;--shiki-everforest-light:#8DA101;--shiki-solarized-light:#2AA198;--shiki-solarized-dark:#2AA198;--shiki-gruvbox-light:#79740E;--shiki-gruvbox-dark:#B8BB26"> ./server</span></span>
<span class="line"><span style="color:#8AADF4;--shiki-catppuccin-light:#1E66F5;--shiki-catppuccin-dark:#8CAAEE;--shiki-everforest-dark:#E69875;--shiki-everforest-light:#F57D26;--shiki-solarized-light:#268BD2;--shiki-solarized-dark:#268BD2;--shiki-gruvbox-light:#427B58;--shiki-gruvbox-dark:#8EC07C">        environment</span><span style="color:#8BD5CA;--shiki-catppuccin-light:#179299;--shiki-catppuccin-dark:#81C8BE;--shiki-everforest-dark:#859289;--shiki-everforest-light:#939F91;--shiki-solarized-light:#657B83;--shiki-solarized-dark:#839496;--shiki-gruvbox-light:#7C6F64;--shiki-gruvbox-dark:#A89984">:</span></span>
<span class="line"><span style="color:#8AADF4;--shiki-catppuccin-light:#1E66F5;--shiki-catppuccin-dark:#8CAAEE;--shiki-everforest-dark:#E69875;--shiki-everforest-light:#F57D26;--shiki-solarized-light:#268BD2;--shiki-solarized-dark:#268BD2;--shiki-gruvbox-light:#427B58;--shiki-gruvbox-dark:#8EC07C">            MAX_FILE_SIZE</span><span style="color:#8BD5CA;--shiki-catppuccin-light:#179299;--shiki-catppuccin-dark:#81C8BE;--shiki-everforest-dark:#859289;--shiki-everforest-light:#939F91;--shiki-solarized-light:#657B83;--shiki-solarized-dark:#839496;--shiki-gruvbox-light:#7C6F64;--shiki-gruvbox-dark:#A89984">:</span><span style="color:#A6DA95;--shiki-catppuccin-light:#40A02B;--shiki-catppuccin-dark:#A6D189;--shiki-everforest-dark:#A7C080;--shiki-everforest-light:#8DA101;--shiki-solarized-light:#2AA198;--shiki-solarized-dark:#2AA198;--shiki-gruvbox-light:#79740E;--shiki-gruvbox-dark:#B8BB26"> 1GB</span></span>
<span class="line"><span style="color:#8AADF4;--shiki-catppuccin-light:#1E66F5;--shiki-catppuccin-dark:#8CAAEE;--shiki-everforest-dark:#E69875;--shiki-everforest-light:#F57D26;--shiki-solarized-light:#268BD2;--shiki-solarized-dark:#268BD2;--shiki-gruvbox-light:#427B58;--shiki-gruvbox-dark:#8EC07C">            UPLOAD_CHUNK_SIZE</span><span style="color:#8BD5CA;--shiki-catppuccin-light:#179299;--shiki-catppuccin-dark:#81C8BE;--shiki-everforest-dark:#859289;--shiki-everforest-light:#939F91;--shiki-solarized-light:#657B83;--shiki-solarized-dark:#839496;--shiki-gruvbox-light:#7C6F64;--shiki-gruvbox-dark:#A89984">:</span><span style="color:#A6DA95;--shiki-catppuccin-light:#40A02B;--shiki-catppuccin-dark:#A6D189;--shiki-everforest-dark:#A7C080;--shiki-everforest-light:#8DA101;--shiki-solarized-light:#2AA198;--shiki-solarized-dark:#2AA198;--shiki-gruvbox-light:#79740E;--shiki-gruvbox-dark:#B8BB26"> 64KB</span></span></code></pre>
                </figure>
            </div>
        </div>
<div class="paragraph">
<p>When deployed, both our server and client applications know how large a file can be, and what size each chunk of the upload must be. The problem, however, is that our client application is built with those hard coded values, and any changes requires re-building and re-deploying it.</p>
</div>
<div class="paragraph">
<p>And that may seem fine since the server would also need to be re-deployed to keep these values in sync, but if we decided to change the poll interval, which doesn&#8217;t affect the server, then we have to go through this again.</p>
</div>
<div class="paragraph">
<p>By the way, in this example the "client" is really just a Nginx image that serves the built artifacts from React.</p>
</div>
</div>
<div class="sect2"><h3 id="_inject_environment_variables_dynamically">Inject Environment Variables Dynamically<a class="anchor" href="#_inject_environment_variables_dynamically">
                    <svg aria-hidden="true">
                        <use href="/sprite.svg#icon-link" />
                    </svg>
                </a></h3>
<div class="paragraph">
<p>Using <code>njs</code> we can modify the request body to inject a piece of JavaScript code containing our global variables:</p>
</div>

<div class="colist arabic">
                <table>
                    <tbody>
                        <tr>
            <td>
                <i class="conum pr-2" data-value="1"></i>
                <b>â¶</b>
            </td>
            <td>The <code>parse</code> function transforms the 64KB string to the number 65536.</td>
        </tr>
                    </tbody>
                </table>
            </div>
<div class="paragraph">
<p>Since it&#8217;s just plain JavaScript we can come in here and change this code at anytime without rebuilding entire application &mdash; a simple reloading of the Nginx process will do.</p>
</div>
</div>
<div class="sect2"><h3 id="_cleaning_up_things_a_little">Cleaning Up Things A Little<a class="anchor" href="#_cleaning_up_things_a_little">
                    <svg aria-hidden="true">
                        <use href="/sprite.svg#icon-link" />
                    </svg>
                </a></h3>
<div class="paragraph">
<p>This works, but we might be slightly annoyed at having to update our variables in two places (the JavaScript file as well as the Docker Compose file).</p>
</div>
<div class="paragraph">
<p>We could try with environment variables, either passed through a <code>.env</code> file or directly through Docker&#8217;s options:</p>
</div>

<span class="line"><span style="color:#8AADF4;--shiki-catppuccin-light:#1E66F5;--shiki-catppuccin-dark:#8CAAEE;--shiki-everforest-dark:#E69875;--shiki-everforest-light:#F57D26;--shiki-solarized-light:#268BD2;--shiki-solarized-dark:#268BD2;--shiki-gruvbox-light:#427B58;--shiki-gruvbox-dark:#8EC07C">        build</span><span style="color:#8BD5CA;--shiki-catppuccin-light:#179299;--shiki-catppuccin-dark:#81C8BE;--shiki-everforest-dark:#859289;--shiki-everforest-light:#939F91;--shiki-solarized-light:#657B83;--shiki-solarized-dark:#839496;--shiki-gruvbox-light:#7C6F64;--shiki-gruvbox-dark:#A89984">:</span></span>
<span class="line"><span style="color:#8AADF4;--shiki-catppuccin-light:#1E66F5;--shiki-catppuccin-dark:#8CAAEE;--shiki-everforest-dark:#E69875;--shiki-everforest-light:#F57D26;--shiki-solarized-light:#268BD2;--shiki-solarized-dark:#268BD2;--shiki-gruvbox-light:#427B58;--shiki-gruvbox-dark:#8EC07C">            context</span><span style="color:#8BD5CA;--shiki-catppuccin-light:#179299;--shiki-catppuccin-dark:#81C8BE;--shiki-everforest-dark:#859289;--shiki-everforest-light:#939F91;--shiki-solarized-light:#657B83;--shiki-solarized-dark:#839496;--shiki-gruvbox-light:#7C6F64;--shiki-gruvbox-dark:#A89984">:</span><span style="color:#A6DA95;--shiki-catppuccin-light:#40A02B;--shiki-catppuccin-dark:#A6D189;--shiki-everforest-dark:#A7C080;--shiki-everforest-light:#8DA101;--shiki-solarized-light:#2AA198;--shiki-solarized-dark:#2AA198;--shiki-gruvbox-light:#79740E;--shiki-gruvbox-dark:#B8BB26"> ./server</span></span>
<span class="line"><span style="color:#8AADF4;--shiki-catppuccin-light:#1E66F5;--shiki-catppuccin-dark:#8CAAEE;--shiki-everforest-dark:#E69875;--shiki-everforest-light:#F57D26;--shiki-solarized-light:#268BD2;--shiki-solarized-dark:#268BD2;--shiki-gruvbox-light:#427B58;--shiki-gruvbox-dark:#8EC07C">        environment</span><span style="color:#8BD5CA;--shiki-catppuccin-light:#179299;--shiki-catppuccin-dark:#81C8BE;--shiki-everforest-dark:#859289;--shiki-everforest-light:#939F91;--shiki-solarized-light:#657B83;--shiki-solarized-dark:#839496;--shiki-gruvbox-light:#7C6F64;--shiki-gruvbox-dark:#A89984">:</span></span>
<span class="line"><span style="color:#8AADF4;--shiki-catppuccin-light:#1E66F5;--shiki-catppuccin-dark:#8CAAEE;--shiki-everforest-dark:#E69875;--shiki-everforest-light:#F57D26;--shiki-solarized-light:#268BD2;--shiki-solarized-dark:#268BD2;--shiki-gruvbox-light:#427B58;--shiki-gruvbox-dark:#8EC07C">            MAX_FILE_SIZE</span><span style="color:#8BD5CA;--shiki-catppuccin-light:#179299;--shiki-catppuccin-dark:#81C8BE;--shiki-everforest-dark:#859289;--shiki-everforest-light:#939F91;--shiki-solarized-light:#657B83;--shiki-solarized-dark:#839496;--shiki-gruvbox-light:#7C6F64;--shiki-gruvbox-dark:#A89984">:</span><span style="color:#A6DA95;--shiki-catppuccin-light:#40A02B;--shiki-catppuccin-dark:#A6D189;--shiki-everforest-dark:#A7C080;--shiki-everforest-light:#8DA101;--shiki-solarized-light:#2AA198;--shiki-solarized-dark:#2AA198;--shiki-gruvbox-light:#79740E;--shiki-gruvbox-dark:#B8BB26"> 1GB</span></span>
<span class="line"><span style="color:#8AADF4;--shiki-catppuccin-light:#1E66F5;--shiki-catppuccin-dark:#8CAAEE;--shiki-everforest-dark:#E69875;--shiki-everforest-light:#F57D26;--shiki-solarized-light:#268BD2;--shiki-solarized-dark:#268BD2;--shiki-gruvbox-light:#427B58;--shiki-gruvbox-dark:#8EC07C">            UPLOAD_CHUNK_SIZE</span><span style="color:#8BD5CA;--shiki-catppuccin-light:#179299;--shiki-catppuccin-dark:#81C8BE;--shiki-everforest-dark:#859289;--shiki-everforest-light:#939F91;--shiki-solarized-light:#657B83;--shiki-solarized-dark:#839496;--shiki-gruvbox-light:#7C6F64;--shiki-gruvbox-dark:#A89984">:</span><span style="color:#A6DA95;--shiki-catppuccin-light:#40A02B;--shiki-catppuccin-dark:#A6D189;--shiki-everforest-dark:#A7C080;--shiki-everforest-light:#8DA101;--shiki-solarized-light:#2AA198;--shiki-solarized-dark:#2AA198;--shiki-gruvbox-light:#79740E;--shiki-gruvbox-dark:#B8BB26"> 64KB</span></span></code></pre>
                </figure>
            </div>
        </div>
<div class="paragraph">
<p>However, the problem with this approach is that Nginx does not inherit the environment variables, and unfortunately none of these values would be available. Unless, that is, you also use the <code>env</code> directive in the main configuration file <em>for each</em> environment variable_:</p>
</div>

<span class="line"><span style="color:#CAD3F5;--shiki-catppuccin-light:#4C4F69;--shiki-catppuccin-dark:#C6D0F5;--shiki-everforest-dark:#D3C6AA;--shiki-everforest-light:#5C6A72;--shiki-solarized-light:#657B83;--shiki-solarized-dark:#839496;--shiki-gruvbox-light:#3C3836;--shiki-gruvbox-dark:#EBDBB2">}</span></span></code></pre>
                </figure>
            </div>
        </div>
<div class="paragraph">
<p>This is not ideal if you have a ton of these variables, but it does mean that you can update their values in just one location. The main downside is that you have to remember to add them here as well.</p>
</div>
<div class="paragraph">
<p>Once you have these variables loaded inside Nginx, you can access them from <code>njs</code> through the <code>process.env</code> object:</p>
</div>

            <td>
                <i class="conum pr-2" data-value="1"></i>
                <b>â¶</b>
            </td>
            <td>We need to convert this object into a string. The client later will have to parse numerical values accordingly.</td>

            </div>
<div class="paragraph">
<p>Since only the environment variables we specified in the Nginx configuration file are available, we can loop freely over the <code>process.env</code> object. We could also add a quick check to ensure only the variables that we&#8217;re interested in are loaded. For example, is not uncommon to prefix them with <code>REACT_APP</code> or <code>VUE_APP</code>.</p>
